New Situation in Disarmament Conference: U.S. Representative Makes First Formal Declaration

Disarmament Convention Should Stipulate Consultation Procedures, British Representative Proposes Acceptance of Chinese Amendments 90

▲Havas Agency, Geneva, 26th: At the Disarmament Conference, the US representative Davis declared to the General Committee this afternoon that the US government felt there was a new situation that should be stipulated in the disarmament convention, the procedures of mutual consultation by the related countries in the case of a violation of the Paris Anti-War Pact. The US wanted that countries, whether or not members of the League of Nations, should strive to maintain peace. This declaration made a very good impression at the meeting.

▲US Advocates Two Points

▲Reuters, Geneva, 26th: US representative Davis made his first formal declaration to the Disarmament Conference General Committee on the disarmament issue today. Several parties regard the US representative's declaration as a precursor to the US presenting more practical disarmament proposals soon. Davis clearly stated the US's desire to cooperate in maintaining peace, saying that the US is prepared to make various great efforts to assist this. The US deeply believes that all countries in the world, especially those in Europe, now want to reduce their arms levels for the first time. He now advocates two things: (1) abolishing offensive weapons; (2) stipulating continuous monitoring. Regarding the second matter, it is appropriate to make the monitoring plans already proposed by various countries more powerful. Davis concluded by saying that the US will have a more precise expression of its best efforts to cooperate in due course.

▲Accepting Our Amendments

The General Committee continued its meeting in the afternoon, resolving to delete the first article of the British disarmament draft. British representative Eden proposed that the committee should accept China's amendments to the draft and form a new amended text, immediately after the fifth article. As of yesterday, Chinese representative Gu Weijun submitted the following amendments: (The signatory countries who are also members of the League of Nations hereby declare that the existing form of the convention does not prejudice the rights and obligations of the members of the League of Nations, nor does it conflict with the powers of the Executive Yuan under the League Covenant.) Eden also proposed accepting China's amendments to Article 4, modifying the number (using war or force to resolve international disputes) to intensify the restrictions on the use of force. It was then decided to hold a main body meeting tomorrow morning, and the next General Committee meeting was scheduled for Friday, when representatives from various countries will submit amendments to the second part of the draft. ▲British Plan Continues Discussion

▲Havas, Geneva, 27th: The Presidium of the Disarmament Conference held a meeting this morning, chaired by Henderson, and resolved to recommend to the General Committee that the first part of the British disarmament plan be postponed for discussion, and that the second part be put forward for discussion first. According to the suggestion of French representative Massigli, the number of committees should speed up their work. The French representative also advocated that the General Assembly elect a special committee, chaired by Greek representative Politis, to study the French proposal for a European mutual assistance pact. This proposal was also passed, and the committee will begin its work soon.

Dutch Cabinet Resigns 91

▲Reuters, The Hague, 26th: The Dutch Cabinet submitted its resignation to the Queen today. The Queen instructed the cabinet members to maintain the status quo as usual. According to current Prime Minister Pieter Sjoerds Gerbrandy, who has been in power since 1929, until today, the recent reason for this was the Lower House's opposition to his economic proposals, and the Social Democratic Party's opposition to handling the mutiny of the Dutch warship Zeven Provinciën. It is expected that the result of the future election will be the establishment of a strong government through the cooperation of various religious groups.

Neurath because his policies lack careful consideration, and Hugenberg because he is too capitalist and has lost the original intention of the National Socialist Party. Duesterberg said that his resignation was really for the sake of the future of the Steel Helmet League. Duesterberg advised the remaining members to do the same and faithfully follow Hitler's guidance.

Painful History of Studying in France

Overseas Chinese Blood Chest Case Drifts Abroad, Killing Each Other, Arresting Officials, Falling into Prison 93

▲Havas Agency, Aix-en-Provence, France, 26th: The sensational Blood Chest Case is being heard by the criminal court here. The details of the case are as follows: Last year, a chest was discovered near here containing a corpse, identified as overseas Chinese Xu Xiangqing (transliteration). After investigation by the police, the criminals Zhang Laiyou, Fu Shanji, and Zhang Hanya (all transliterations), all friends of the deceased, were arrested. Zhang Hanya and two others died of tuberculosis in Marseille prison. Only Zhang Laiyou remains, charged with complicity in murder. Laiyou is short, skinny, and dying. Everyone believes that this case will probably end by itself before the trial. At the hearing today, Zhang Laiyou's testimony was interpreted by an interpreter. The judge first reviewed the facts of the case. The victim in this case was a peddler of odds and ends who earned a lot of profit. Zhang Laiyou, Fu Shanji, and Zhang Hanya knew that he had a lot of savings, so they lured him to a certain place and killed him. According to the defendant's confession, Fu Shanji killed him with a hammer, and before Fu Shanji died, he said that Xu Xiangqing threatened him with a pistol, and he had to defend himself. The judge asked Zhang Laiyou if this was the case, and Zhang Laiyou replied that the murder weapon was not purchased by him. When the incident happened, he was sleeping at home, and Fu and others suddenly came and told him what had happened. Fearing involvement in the case, he fled with Fu and others. The court determined that Zhang Laiyou was guilty of complicity in murder and theft and sentenced him to 20 years in prison.

Japanese Troops Change Harassment Tactics

Japanese Troops Secretly Moved North from Luandong, Concentrating Forces to Attack Nantianmen 94

A special dispatch from Beiping states that after the Japanese army occupied Luandong, they turned to attack Nantianmen, threatening Beiping and Tianjin. It was originally hoped that they could quickly capture the Nantianmen fortress to attack Miyun and disrupt the rear of Beiping and Tianjin, trapping our eastern army in a heavy siege. Fortunately, our army resisted bravely, fighting fiercely for four or five days and nights without the enemy succeeding. Furthermore, due to heavy casualties, the original forces were feeling inadequate. Therefore, they changed their strategy, transferring all the Japanese troops from Luandong to the north to reinforce their position. The Luandong area was temporarily guarded by the puppet army of Li Jichun. At the same time, they declared to the outside world that they had no intention of invading beyond the Great Wall, withdrawing from the Great Wall to confuse international opinion. Their plan is truly cunning. The Japanese army's transfer from northern Luandong began around the 30th. By dawn on the 23rd, all Japanese troops from the Qian'an and Lulong areas had been completely withdrawn. During the withdrawal, they occasionally bombarded our positions with field guns, creating a false impression of attempting to cross the river and advance, to prevent us from discovering the truth. Unexpectedly, on the evening of the 22nd, a unit of puppet troops surrendered to Gao Guizi's army, leaking the secret. Gao then commanded his troops to cross the river and launch a counterattack on the morning of the 23rd, and they soon recovered Qian'an. The He and Wang armies, upon hearing the news, also coordinated to advance. The Wang army occupied Lulong, and the He army advanced to Anshan. This morning (25th), the He army has approached Changli. The Gao and Wang armies are also gradually advancing north from Qian'an and Lulong. Currently, order has been restored in Qian'an and Lulong, and personnel from various agencies are returning from Beiping and Tianjin to their counties to work. A unit of the Japanese army is deploying defenses in the Jianchangying area, only a few dozen miles away from our army. It is expected that a temporary stalemate will form in that area.

On the Gubeikou front, after the Japanese army occupied Koumen, our army guarded the Nantianmen, Badaolouzi, and two gun tower positions, surrounding Gubeikou on three sides, forming a semi-circle. The Nantianmen front position is in a dangerous location and has strong defenses. Badaolouzi is on the left flank of Nantianmen, one times higher than Nantianmen, forming a mutually supporting formation. There are eight artillery towers on it, hence the name Badaolouzi (Eight Tower Buildings). The gain or loss of this location is extremely important. The Japanese army began its attack at dawn on the 21st, adopting a strategy of flanking from the left and right, launching a combined attack of infantry, artillery, and air force on the Badaolouzi, two gun tower, and Longtangou areas. The battle for Badaolouzi was particularly fierce. The positions were gained and lost five or six times in four or five days and nights of bloody fighting. Our army killed over three thousand enemy soldiers. Our army lost two battalion commanders and three were wounded. Soldiers casualties numbered three to four thousand. The fighting remained extremely fierce yesterday (24th) and today (25th). At 6:00 AM yesterday, the enemy used six aircraft and concentrated artillery fire to bombard the left flank of Nantianmen, and over two thousand infantrymen launched attacks on Nantianmen and our left flank. The two sides engaged in fierce fighting, with hand-to-hand combat occurring five or six times. Around 10:00 AM, our left flank suffered heavy casualties and was also under pressure from a large number of enemy reinforcements. The left flank position was once lost, but a certain unit was mobilized to launch a brave counterattack, charging five times. At 12:00 PM, they repelled the enemy and regained the original position. At 3:00 PM in the afternoon, the Japanese army launched another large-scale attack on our front. Our army responded calmly, and the enemy did not succeed. At night, the enemy bombarded us with heavy artillery, and the sound of artillery fire continued all night. All the towers were completely destroyed. The Japanese army launched another charge this morning and are currently engaged in fierce fighting. The Japanese army's intention is to break through the Nantianmen position, advance on Miyun, and threaten Beiping and Tianjin. (April 25th)

Fu Zuoyi and Others Arrive in Gan

Conferring with Chiang on Emergency Anti-Japanese Military Affairs, Wu Jingheng and Li Yuying Also Arrive in Gan 95

A dispatch from Nanchang states that representatives from the Jin, Sui, and Chahar armies, Fu Zuoyi; representatives from the Northeast generals, Zhang Xueming; and representatives from the Beiping Military Affairs Commission, Zhu Guangmu, arrived in Gan with important missions to pay respects to Chairman Chiang. They arrived in Xun on the 24th from Ping and immediately took a special train to the province. They arrived at Nanchang Station at 12:00 PM. The General Headquarters and the Provincial Government both sent liaison officers to the station to welcome and take care of them. After Fu and others crossed the river into the city, they took cars to the Science Museum to meet with Chiang. They reported in detail on the anti-Japanese military situation and represented the military and civilians of North China in requesting Chiang to go north immediately to take unified command to save the critical situation. It is reported that Chiang expressed his appreciation to the officers and soldiers fighting in North China and promised to go north in the shortest possible time. He also gave instructions on the combat plan for the Luan River and the Great Wall, as well as the defense of Beiping and Tianjin. Fu and others telegraphed the situation of their meeting with Chiang to senior military officers in North China that evening. It is reported that Chiang will convene He Guoguang, He Chengjun, and senior staff at the headquarters to further discuss military matters in order to make urgent responses. According to sources at the headquarters, Chiang has decided to increase the deployment of fresh troops to various lines due to the urgency of the military situation in North China. As for the timing of Chiang's trip north, it may have to be slightly delayed because the Red bandits have recently concentrated their main forces in the upper reaches of the Fu River in Yile, repeatedly attacking Fu. This is because the Guangdong and Guangxi armies have not fired a single arrow or bullet at the pseudo-central area of the Red bandits in Yudu, Xingguo, and Ruijin, allowing the bandits to have no worries about their rear. Therefore, Chiang has been urging Chen Jitang and Li Zongren to implement the suppression of the bandits and not to hesitate any longer. The written and telegraphic communications are as urgent as shooting stars. At the same time, he also telegraphed Cai Tingkai in Guangdong, strongly arguing the advantages and disadvantages of suppressing the bandits, so as to avoid mutual destruction. Currently, the anti-Japanese military situation urgently relies on Chiang's leadership in the north. The timing of Chiang's trip north depends on whether the suppression of the Red bandits can be abandoned. Whether the suppression of the Red bandits can be abandoned depends on whether Guangdong and Guangxi are willing to send a large number of troops to Gan to assist in the suppression, so as to attack the bandits' rear. If Chen and Li are willing to send a large number of troops to attack Yudu and Xingguo, and simultaneously act with Fujian, Jiangxi, and Hunan, then the encirclement will be complete. The suppression of the Red bandits will not be a problem, and Chiang can immediately go north to fight the Japanese. This is what is meant by the southwest being fully responsible for the suppression of the Red bandits, and the central government being fully responsible for the anti-Japanese war.

Wu Zhihui and Li Shizeng arrived in Jiujiang from Beijing on the 25th and immediately took the Nanxun Railway to the province. After getting off the train, they took a ferry across the river and then switched to cars to rush to the Science Museum to meet with Chairman Chiang. It is reported that they were discussing the temporary meeting of the Kuomintang and the anti-Japanese military situation, and plan to stay for one or two days before returning to Beijing. (April 25th)

Setting Up Anti-Japanese Vanguard Headquarters in Guangzhou, Cai and Chen Have Decided on Various Implementation Plans 96

Verdict Announced in Chen Peng Case

Chen Peng and Others Declare Dissatisfaction and Decide to Appeal, Liang Youguang and Wang Jiantang Acquitted and Released 97

The case of Chen Duxiu, Peng Shuzhi, and others, leaders of the Trotskyist faction of the Chinese Communist Party, endangering the Republic of China, has been fully tried by the Jiangsu High Court's Criminal Division of the Jiangning Local Court on the 14th, 15th, and 20th of this month. The verdict was announced at 1:30 PM on the 26th in the original court. Presiding Judge Hu Shancheng, Judges Lin Zhemin and Zhang Bingci, Clerk Shen Yuren, and Prosecutor Zhu Jun, and others took the stand. First, the clerk announced the court's verdict today in the case of Chen Duxiu and others endangering the Republic of China. The judge then ordered Chen Duxiu, Peng Shuzhi, Wang Ziping, He Afang, Wang Wu, Pu Yifan, Wang Zhaoqun, Guo Jinghao, Liang Youguang, and Wang Jiantang to be brought to court. Judge Hu read out the main text of the verdict (listed separately). He then informed the defendants that if they were not satisfied with the verdict, they would be allowed to appeal. Except for Liang Youguang and Wang Jiantang, who were acquitted, all eight of Chen Duxiu and others declared their dissatisfaction and decided to appeal. Judge Hu then informed them that they would be allowed to appeal within ten days of the service of the judgment. He then immediately announced the adjournment, and the defendants were returned to custody. It is reported that Liang Youguang and Wang Jiantang will be released after finding guarantors.

Main Text of the Verdict 98

The second criminal court of the Jiangsu High Court publicly announces the main text of the verdict in the case of Chen Duxiu and others endangering the Republic of China. (Chen Duxiu and Peng Shuzhi are each sentenced to thirteen years of imprisonment and fifteen years of deprivation of civil rights for jointly using writing to promote the overthrow of the country. Wang Ziping and He Afang are each sentenced to five years of imprisonment and seven years of deprivation of civil rights for assisting in the overthrow of the country with writing. Wang Wu, Pu Yifan, and Wang Zhaoqun are each sentenced to five years of imprisonment and seven years of deprivation of civil rights for organizing a group with the aim of endangering the Republic of China. Guo Jinghao is sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment and three years of deprivation of civil rights for organizing a group with the aim of endangering the Republic of China. The number of days of pre-trial detention is allowed to be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. Items related to the crime, as well as books and printed materials found in the case, are confiscated. Liang Youguang and Wang Jiantang are found not guilty.)

Life in Prison 99

Chen and Peng share a room. When reporters visited, the two had just returned to the detention center from court. They were smoking and reading newspapers in the room, wearing short coats and their heads uncovered, and their attitude was very relaxed. The room contained two beds, a table, and a bookshelf, which were full of social science books, resembling the dormitory life of a university student. Upon seeing the reporters, both of them stood up and greeted them with smiles, as if welcoming the arrival of friends, making it hard to believe that they were prisoners.

Chen and Peng Talk 100

When asked about their thoughts after the verdict, Chen replied, "The court's decision is exactly what we expected, so there is nothing surprising about it." After saying this, a dim smile was exchanged on his dark face. Peng replied, "We were sentenced for violating Article 6 and Article 2, Section 2 of the Emergency Law on Punishing Those Who Endanger the Republic of China, but we have never been able to find any serious facts of treason in our past actions. The group exercising the power to rule can never be regarded as the country." The reporter asked, "Are you both preparing to appeal?" Chen replied, "After the judgment is officially served, we will appeal to the extent possible. As for whether to ask the original lawyers to defend us, we have not yet thought about it." (Central News Agency)

The Lunantai Weir Road in Southern Shandong is About to Be Completed

Connecting the Jinpu, Jiaoji, Longhai, and Yanwei Roads, the Weixian-Juxian Section Has Been Completed and Opened to Traffic 101

A dispatch from Jinan states that the Jinpu Road runs vertically through Shandong Province from north to south, and the Jiaoji Road runs from Qingdao to Jinan, connecting with the Jinpu Road, forming a T-shape, making north-south and east-west transportation fairly convenient. Since the year before last, the Department of Construction has been actively expanding motor vehicle roads, and the eastern, western, and northern Shandong lines, extending in all directions, have been completed. Southern Shandong is more difficult to build due to the complex mountain ranges and has not yet been built. However, the Taizhuang-Weixian line has long been surveyed and planned. This line can connect the Jinpu, Jiaoji, Longhai, and Yanwei roads, which has a significant relationship with commerce and culture. The Taiyi District Motor Vehicle Road Bureau of the Department of Construction was ordered to start construction last year. So far, the Weixian-Juxian section has been completed first and opened to traffic on the 24th of this month. It is also being built westward to Taierzhuang. The entire line is 800 miles long, passing through Linyi, Juxian, Zhucheng, and Anqiu. The road surface is more than four meters wide (one meter wider than the Yanwei Road). There are many bridges along the way. If permanent bridges are built, it will cost 1.5 million yuan. The cost of building temporary bridges is also 810,000 yuan. The provincial government has approved that the money will be temporarily advanced by the local area and reimbursed later. It is expected that it will take 11 hours to reach Taizhuang when the Taizhuang-Weixian line opens to traffic. If the bridges are repaired, it will only take 9 hours. If guests from the south want to go to Yantai or Qingdao, they no longer need to detour through Jinan. They can get off the train at Xin'anzhen on the Longhai Road, take a car through Tancheng to Linyi, and then take the Taiwei car to Weixian to go to Qingdao or Yantai, which is very convenient. The Jinpu Road has a branch line in Lincheng that passes through Zaozhuang to Taizhuang (the Zao-Tai section currently only transports coal). If passenger cars are allowed, passengers on the Jinpu Road can get off at Taizhuang, take the Taiwei car to Weixian in the morning, and take the Yanwei car to Yantai, arriving at 8:00 PM. Traveling through half of Shandong Province for 1,400 miles will only take this shortest time, which saves a day compared to detouring through Jinan. It can be said to be extremely convenient. The car fare for each line of motor vehicle road in this province is generally from 2.5 to 3 cents per mile. Now, Wang Yimin, director of the Taiyi District Motor Vehicle Road Bureau, has submitted to the Department of Construction for approval to reduce the car fare on the Taiwei Road to 2 cents per mile. The current car fare for the Weixian-Juxian section that has opened to traffic is 7.7 yuan. If the entire line is completed, it will cost more than 15 yuan, which is more economical than other lines. This road has a major mission for the future commercial and cultural development of southern Shandong. (April 25th)

Songjiang: Tragic Death Due to Lost Love 102

Juanbao, the daughter of Wang An-sheng, the owner of Wang Anji Hat Shop south of the Chang Bridge in this city, had married a man named Zhong. After her husband died, she had an affair with Yang Zhenbo, a monk from Sichuan in the Doumu Pavilion. Their interactions became intimate, and they lived together. The monk exhausted all his savings and went to live in Hankou with the woman, and they had two children. Recently, the monk ran out of money, and Juanbao quickly returned to her mother's house. However, the monk wanted to live with her, but her parents firmly refused. The monk was filled with resentment and conceived the idea of ​​ending his life, hanging himself in front of the hat shop. This morning (27th), someone discovered it and reported it to the prosecutor's office for verification. It was confirmed that he had hanged himself to death. The Wang family was instructed to collect the body.

Suzhou: Execution of Lake Bandit Leader 104

Hong Wanwu, the leader of the Henan gang of bandits in Taihu Lake, is 57 years old this year. The year before last, he gathered a crowd to kidnap a woman named Zhou Tangshi in Zhenze Township. He used a towel to wrap her face and raped her three times. Later, police detectives from Wujiang County arrested Hong in Wuxi. After interrogation, he confessed to committing numerous crimes, including tying up and raping Tangshi and others. The record of the confession was submitted to the High Court, which requested the provincial government to pass a resolution to secretly order the original county to carry out the execution by shooting. The Sheng family estate in Biling has long been approved by the Executive Yuan to return the Sheng family's Liuyuan Villa Ancestral Hall in Suzhou and properties and sacrificial fields in various places, as well as the Sheng family's public ancestral hall on Gushan at the Xiling Bridge in Hangzhou and nearby fields. Request for Funds to Protect Dams 108

The Gaochun East Dam is located upstream on the border between Liyang and Gaochun counties. It is of great importance to the water conservancy of seven counties, including Wujin, Wuxi, Wuxian, Wujiang, Changshu, and Liyang. When the Jiangsu Construction Department was building the Jingjian Road, it was stipulated that the original line would pass through the collapsed dam head of the East Dam and go straight to Anhui. Li Yuansheng, who was entrusted by Liyang to manage the dam head, and more than one hundred shops organized a petition group and sent Fu Tingjing and other representatives to Beijing Province to petition for a change of line. The Construction Department then approved the line to be rerouted east of the dam, adding 78,000 cubic meters of earthwork and building two more bridges, costing a total of 15,000 yuan. The provincial government and the Construction Department designated that the local area should raise 5,000 yuan. The New Line Committee of the East Dam decided that the cost should be borne jointly by the relevant counties and documents were prepared to appoint Fu Tingjing, Shi Dezhong, and others to contact Suzhou, Changzhou, Wuxi, and other counties to negotiate for the allocation of funds to assist. Wuxi has transferred the letter from the Chamber of Commerce to the county government for submission to the county administration meeting to consider the allocation of funds to assist.

Changzhou: Gangsters Commit Revenge Killing and Robbery 109

Wang Qichang, a farmer in Zhoujiaqiao Village, Liutang Township, Third District of Wuyi, has always been targeted by local bad people. Unexpectedly, at about 1:00 AM on the 26th, six or seven robbers suddenly broke into his house, tied up Qichang and his wife, Zhu, and beat them with weapons, causing injuries all over their bodies. Then they looted a small amount of clothing and left. After the incident, the injured were sent to the Wujin Hospital in the city for treatment. Zhu's ribs had been broken and she was on the verge of death. Wang Qichang was seriously injured. According to the locals, the gangsters may have been motivated by revenge, hence the viciousness of their actions.

Zhenjiang: Trial of Township Chief's Embezzlement of Treasury Bonds Opens 110

Ling Chaobai, the village chief of Shangdang Township in Licun, was ordered in the 19th year of the Republic of China to solicit 78 yuan in treasury bonds, which had been outstanding for a long time. Previously, due to a feud with someone, Tang Deji reported that Ling was suspected of embezzling treasury bonds. He then raised Zhu Changren, Ling Bingren, Ling Guang'er, and Wei Zhengshi as witnesses and sued him in court for fraud. The prosecutor's office had concluded the investigation and considered that Ling Chaobai was suspected of committing a crime, so he was taken into custody and publicly prosecuted. Yesterday, Liao the judge presided over the public trial at the Criminal Division. Ling and the witnesses were summoned to the court to be examined one by one. Lawyer Fang, who was appointed by Ling, appeared in court and argued for a long time. The judge adjourned the case and set the date for the verdict on May 2. Ling was returned to custody, and the others were dismissed.

Changshu: Silver and Money Industry Switches to Using Foreign Standards 111

Since the National Government issued an order to abolish taels and switch to yuan in the silver and money industry, various places have followed suit one after another. The silver and money industry in the county held a meeting on the 26th to discuss the matter. It was unanimously decided to follow the Suzhou agreement to implement the abolition of [ ] from May 1. All transactions, deposits, etc. will be changed to foreign codes.

Nantong: Tonghai and Qidong Jointly Dredge and Widen the Xinkin River 112

The Department of Construction considers the Xinkin River to be the main river for draining water from Nantong, Haimen, and Qidong counties. In recent years, it has been silted up and impassable. Therefore, the department sent engineer Yu Wei to Tong to convene responsible representatives from the three counties to discuss the joint dredging issue. It was decided that the cost of the project would be borne by the benefited fields in the three counties, and construction will begin on May 1.

Hefei: Excavation of Ancient Tomb from the Eastern Han Dynasty Begins 113

The public organizations of Hefei have complied with provincial orders and jointly formed the Ancient Tomb Development Supervision Committee to excavate the ancient tomb of the Eastern Han Dynasty seven miles east of the city. A large number of workers were hired and began excavating on the 22nd. However, due to the large area, it was difficult to find the tomb door for a while, so the search continued on the 23rd. A large number of people came out of the city to watch. The tomb bricks were as large as city bricks, the material was extremely fine, and there were swirling patterns on them. Many coins from the Han Dynasty were also found. It was undoubtedly a Han tomb.

Jiaxing: Verdict Announced in Case Against Xu, Chief of the Branch Bureau 114

Xu Hongxiang, chief of the Xinrong Township Public Security Branch Bureau in Jiaxing, arrested and detained the calligrapher Yang Xiaochun at the request of Shen Xinru of the Township Chamber of Commerce. Then, someone bailed Yang out. Yang was unwilling to be detained for no reason, so he filed a complaint with the Jiaxing Local Branch Court accusing Xu and Shen of hindering freedom. After the investigation was not prosecuted, Yang applied for reconsideration. The High Court ordered a reinvestigation and the prosecutor filed a public prosecution in accordance with the crime of hindering freedom. After interrogation, the judge ordered them to each post a bail of 100 yuan to go outside. The case has now been finalized and the verdict was announced yesterday: Shen Xinru and Xu Hongxiang are not guilty.

If the Key to the Northern Gate is Not Hot River, It Will Not Be Solid; If the Situation in Hebei is Not Western Liaoning, It Will Not Be Complete 115

The name of joint management is difficult to endure, and the strategy of defending the border lacks good plans. If you want to rely solely on the Great Wall, you don't have the strength of Qin Huang, and if you want to steal peace, you don't have the talent of Qin Hui. Then, other than selecting generals, sharpening soldiers, and plotting further development, what is the benefit of cutting off the name of resistance to the point of being utterly hopeless? Fortunately, the morale of the soldiers is still strong, and the remaining courage has not waned. The two roads out of the army are just about to meet. Although the three eastern provinces are difficult to restore by force, these two places must be fought to the death. If this cannot be done, the shame of losing land cannot be removed, and the crime of the authorities misleading the country cannot be redeemed. The Emperor's Axe is in front, and I hope to be warned and introspected."

The Shanghai Municipal Council Attempts to Seize Factory Inspection Rights

The Municipal Government Sent a Letter Yesterday to the Consulates-General Requesting Rectification, and Three National Products Organizations Objected 120

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession passed the amendment to Article 34 of the bylaws of the Yangjingbang Regulations at the recent Special Meeting of Western Taxpayers, attempting to seize the management rights of factories within the concession. Mayor Wu and the Chinese Ratepayers Association, among others, have made earnest statements. The Municipal Council's move violates the Land Regulations. At 10:00 AM yesterday, the Municipal Government formally sent a letter to the Consuls-General of various countries stationed in Shanghai, requesting correction. The original letter is excerpted below:

To whom it may concern: Factory inspection is an integral part of our national labor administration. Since the promulgation of the Factory Law by the National Government, this government has repeatedly sent personnel to negotiate with the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession regarding the inspection of factories within the jurisdiction, but no agreement has been reached. Now, the Municipal Council, knowing that it has no right to manage the factories within the concession according to the Yangjingbang Regulations, has adopted the method of amending Article 34 of the bylaws to attempt to obtain the right to inspect factories. This government is deeply surprised. The concession is Chinese territory, and the people within the concession have the same obligation to obey the laws of their country as the people residing outside the concession. It is not permissible for the concession authorities to exclude the people within the concession from the jurisdiction of their own country by means of a resolution. The legal status of the concession is very clear, and the powers of the Municipal Council are also limited. Now, attempting to obtain a legal basis for managing factories by adding bylaws is absurd. Factory inspection is established to implement labor policies, and its purpose is to promote the sound development of the national economy, which is different from local governance. Even based on the Yangjingbang Regulations, Article 9, which states "Planning governance for proper management," lists specific matters of governance rather than providing a general scope. Even if there are bylaws, they cannot exceed the scope of the items listed in the regulations; otherwise, they would conflict with Article 11 of the regulations. Such abuse of power not only infringes upon national sovereignty but also violates the treaties signed between China and various countries. This government, in consideration of respecting national legal rights and protecting the interests of labor, lodges a protest against this ultra vires and illegal act of the Municipal Council. In addition to sending separate letters, a corresponding letter is sent, hoping for your careful consideration, prompt correction, and a reply. To the Consuls-General of various countries stationed in Shanghai.

Remarks from a Person in Charge of the Ministry of Industry 121

Regarding the case of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession attempting to seize factory inspection rights, according to a person in charge of the Ministry of Industry, the ministry and the Central People's Movement Committee have sent personnel to Shanghai to discuss response measures with the Shanghai Municipal Government. A protest has been lodged with the Shanghai Consular Body. If there are no satisfactory results, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs will lodge representations with the ministers of the related countries stationed in China. Furthermore, our country's representatives will raise this case at the upcoming International Labour Conference, seeking international judgment.

Meetings of Two National Products Organizations 122

The Shanghai Citizens' Association for Promoting National Products and the China National Products Maintenance Association held a joint meeting at 3:00 PM yesterday in the grand hall of the association in Jiu Mu Di to oppose the Municipal Council's seizure of our country's factory inspection. Representatives from factories such as Yapu Er Electric Factory, Tian Yi Wei Mother Factory, Yili Soda Factory, and Huayang Dyeing and Weaving Factory, including Xu Tingzuo, Hu Xiyuan, Zhang Zilian, and Wang Xingyi, totaling over fifty people, attended. Chen Yiting presided over the meeting, reporting on the purpose of the meeting and the process of the Special Meeting of Western Taxpayers amending the Land Regulations to authorize the Municipal Council to manage factories. Then, discussions began. Sun Daosheng, Zhu Dechao, Chen Binghui, Wang Xingyi, and others successively expressed their opinions and resolved: (1) Send a letter to the Municipal Government requesting serious representations to strive for national rights, with the association leading all national products factories in Shanghai as a pledge of support. (2) Send letters to various national products organizations to form a committee to oppose the Municipal Council's inspection of factories, and publicly elect Chen Binghui, Chen Yiting, Wang Xingyi, Sun Daosheng, Xu Genghua, Wang Jiean, and Wu Zhihao as representatives, designating Wang Xingyi and Chen Yiting as conveners. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.

Declaration of the National Products Factory Association 123

The Shanghai National Products Factory Association issued a declaration yesterday, stating: The amendment to Article 34 of the bylaws of the Land Regulations passed by the Shanghai Public Concession Western Ratepayers' Meeting on the 19th of this month, regarding the management of factories within the concession, not only attempts to seize factory inspection rights but is also essentially a destruction of our country's sovereignty, a severance of our country's laws, and a conflict with international conventions. The Factory Law and the Factory Inspection Law are complete national laws and cannot be compared to local government's single regulations. Although the Municipal Council is a de facto autonomous body, it absolutely has no right to our country's national laws. Knowing that it has no right to handle factory management, it uses the clever method of amending the bylaws at the Western Ratepayers' Meeting, which can be described as doing everything possible to deceive the heavens and change the earth. The original text of Article 34 of the bylaws of the Land Regulations stipulates that small vegetable markets, clubs, billiard rooms, restaurants, etc., opened within the concession must obtain licenses from it; otherwise, they will be subject to fines. This has nothing to do with factory management. How can it be far-fetched and combined into one matter to gain unlimited real power that has never existed before? Moreover, Chinese residents in the Public Concession account for more than 95%, while Westerners account for less than 5%. Chinese residents pay 55% of the taxes, while Westerners pay 45%. As fellow citizens, even if the Western Ratepayers' Meeting strongly argues and insists on amending, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association's general meeting has already resolved to oppose it, and in terms of legal principles, the majority should be followed. This association, as a group of national products factories, absolutely opposes this kind of illegal and unreasonable behavior that attempts to seize factory inspection rights. This declaration is hereby issued.

Korean Inventors Invent Electric Anti-Aircraft Gun; Ministry of Military Affairs Orders Approval for Manufacturing 124

According to China East News Agency, since the tyrannical Japanese planes have wreaked havoc, people in the country have gradually paid attention to air defense. In recent days, some people have invented flying arrows and flying thunder, but their firing power is not as good as that of anti-aircraft guns, and the results are not significant. Recently, two Koreans who have become naturalized Chinese citizens have invented an electric anti-aircraft gun that can fire up to twenty English miles, reaching 10,000 meters. The highest flying aircraft only flies to 5,000 meters, so if this new weapon is successfully tested, it can hit aircraft with ease. A reporter from the China East News Agency went to various places to inquire and will record the details below.

Overview of Purchase and Manufacturing 125

The inventors of this weapon are also Korean. Its structure is similar to that of an anti-aircraft gun, but it adds two devices, namely a small mirror and two electric boxes. When firing bullets, it relies entirely on electricity, and when aiming at aircraft, a small mirror is also required (Ordinary anti-aircraft guns have one small mirror, while this type of electric anti-aircraft gun has two small mirrors, making it more convenient to aim at aircraft).

Enemy Plots to Buy It 126

When the two Koreans invented the gun, the Japanese government became aware of it and paid great attention. It then sent people to buy it, willing to negotiate with the Koreans to purchase it for one million yuan. The two Koreans were hesitating when He Shiping, who had served as a staff officer of the Jiangbei guerrilla commander, found out. He tried his best to win them over and urged them to serve the country. At that time, he drafted a memorial and reported it to the National Government, requesting a trial manufacturing. The National Government then ordered it to be directly submitted to the Ministry of Military Affairs for approval. On the first of this month, when Wang Jingwei arrived in Shanghai, He personally visited him at Chu Minyi's residence. Wang quite agreed with this electric anti-aircraft gun.

Military Department Approves 127

According to He himself, he had reported the construction situation of the Korean gun to the Ministry of Military Affairs, and now he has received the department's Bing She Zi No. 317 approval. The original text reads: "Received, please draw detailed diagrams and submit them directly to this department for review." This is the approval.

The Gun's Effectiveness 128

He said that the gun's effectiveness is extremely great. All aircraft in the air, regardless of how high they fly, can be destroyed. Furthermore, if the gun's internal parts are installed in torpedo boats, submarines can be attacked. If installed in ordinary artillery, it can shoot at very distant enemies. He has now submitted a request to the Ministry of Military Affairs for the allocation of funds for manufacturing. If approved, a trial manufacturing can be carried out.

Cen Chunxuan Died in Shanghai Yesterday

Survived by Five Sons and Four Daughters; Funeral Set for Today; Cen Held Prominent Positions and Lived to 73 138

According to Guo Wen News Agency, Cen Chunxuan, former Governor-General of Liangguang and one of the seven presidents of the Constitutional Protection Government, has been residing in Shanghai for twelve years since abandoning political life in 1920. Cen had a history of heart disease, and ten days ago, he suddenly suffered a stroke. Despite the efforts of famous Chinese and Western doctors, he passed away at 7:20 AM yesterday (the 27th) at his residence at No. 104 Siming Village, Foch Road, Shanghai, at the age of 73. When reporters visited Cen's residence, a shed was being built. A Cen's Funeral Office was set up at No. 106 on the left side of his residence. The funeral is scheduled for today. The details of his survivors and his brief biography are recorded below.

Survivors and Near Relatives 139

Cen held prominent positions in the late Qing Dynasty and the early Republic of China, and was famous throughout the country. He was the son of Cen Xiangqin, the former Governor-General of Yunnan and Guizhou. There were five brothers, and Cen Chunxuan was the third. Only Cen Chunming is still alive, and the rest have passed away early. Cen Chunming was the former Governor of Hunan in the Qing Dynasty and is now also in Shanghai. Cen's first wife passed away long ago, and he now has four concubines, all of whom are concubines. He is survived by five sons and four daughters. The eldest son is Deguang, the second is Delin, the third is Detian, the fourth is Dezhao, and the fifth is Dehong. All but Dehong are adults. The eldest daughter, Dezhen, married into the Chen family, the second daughter, Dejing, married into the Kang family, the third daughter, Defu, returned to the Xu family, and the fourth daughter, Dehan, is currently studying at a certain school and is still unmarried. All family members are in Shanghai. According to his family, whether the coffin will be transported back to his ancestral home in Guilin for burial after the funeral today (i.e., today) has not yet been decided.

Brief Biography of Cen 140

Cen, named Chunxuan and styled Yunjie, was a native of Xilin County, Guangxi. During the late Qing Dynasty, he served as a provincial commander and was successively promoted to Governor of Guangdong, Governor-General of Liangguang, Governor-General of Yunnan and Guizhou, and Governor-General of Sichuan. He was then transferred to the Minister of Posts and Communications, rising rapidly and becoming famous for a time. Finally, the Qing court sent Cen to mediate the Sichuan-Hankou Railway dispute. Before long, the Xinhai Revolution broke out. With the founding of the Republic of China, Cen's thinking was relatively new. He once served as the Director-General of the Hubei-Guangdong Railway. Later, Yuan Shikai plotted to usurp the throne and changed the title to Hongxian. Cen strongly opposed it, so Yuan ordered his arrest. Cen then fled to Nanyang. After Yuan's death, Cen returned to China. In 1917, when Duan Qirui formed a cabinet, Cen went to the southwest the following year and formed an extraordinary parliament and constitutional protection government in Guangdong. At that time, Cen was one of the seven presidents, including Premier Sun, Tang Shaoyi, Wu Tingfang, and Lu Rongting. In 1920, the Guangdong and Guangxi factions fought for power, and Cen was the leader of the Guangxi faction. Later, the Guangdong faction gained power, and Guangxi province also came under the control of the Guangdong faction. Cen fled to Shanghai as a resident. At that time, Cen was old, so he decided to retire to Shanghai and spend the rest of his years reading poetry and books, no longer seeking a living in politics. After twelve years, in 1922, the Northern Government still awarded Cen the First Class Grand Ribbon Baoguang Jiahe Medal.

Xiao Zhenying Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning; The Results of His Meeting with Chiang in Jiangxi Were Exceptionally Satisfactory 141

Xiao Zhenying, the representative of Song Zheyuan, commander of the 29th Army, went to Jiangxi to meet with Chairman Chiang to report on defense matters and to ask for instructions. It is now known that Xiao arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning via Beijing and made contacts with various circles. The results of Xiao's trip to Jiangxi were exceptionally satisfactory. He is scheduled to go north in two or three days to meet with Commander Song and report everything.

The Fourth Batch of Antiquities Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon

Still Stored in the Building on Catholic Church Street; Totaling 6,267 Boxes 142

The fourth batch of cultural relics from the Palace Museum, totaling 6,267 boxes, escorted by Ma Heng, deputy director of the Palace Museum, and others, arrived in Pukou on the 23rd on three trains. After unloading, they were loaded onto the Jianguo ship and sailed to Shanghai at 2:00 PM on the 26th. They arrived in Shanghai at 11:00 AM yesterday and berthed at the Jinliyuan Wharf. Unloading began in the afternoon and was still stored in the building at No. 26 Catholic Church Street. It is said that unloading will not be completed until the 29th. The fifth batch of cultural relics is expected to arrive in about a week. The details are recorded below.

Number of Cultural Relics 143

The fourth batch of cultural relics includes 4,639 boxes from the Palace Museum, 1,400 boxes from the Cultural Relics Preservation Institute of the Ministry of Interior, and 228 boxes from the Summer Palace, totaling 6,267 boxes. These include many bronzes, books, and porcelain, as well as eleven Qin and Han Dynasty stone drums and a bronze cannon from the 27th year of the Kangxi reign.

Arrived in Port in the Morning 144

The Jianguo ship arrived at the Jinliyuan Wharf at 11:00 AM. After receiving the news, the Municipal Public Security Bureau immediately sent Deputy Inspector-General Dong Pingyu, Inspectors Cheng Fengyi, Kong Qingnan, Zhang Zhishan, and twelve others to take care of the wharf. The French Concession Police also sent French and Chinese detectives and patrolmen to set up posts around the wharf and maintain strict security.

Escorting Personnel 145

When this batch of cultural relics left Peiping on the 23rd, it was escorted to Pukou by Ma Heng, deputy director of the Palace Museum, and more than ten staff members. Director Ma took a car to Shanghai first to make contact. The Executive Yuan sent Councilor Chen Rui, Dispatch Section Chief Wang Jinliang, and staff member Zhai Zonghan, and the Ministry of Interior sent Section Chief Zhang Guogan and Cao Zhonglin to escort them. The Military Police Headquarters also sent Inspector Liu Yingjie and Company Commander Zhao Zhong to lead a company of infantry and a platoon of machine guns to provide close protection along the ship.

Unloaded in the Afternoon 146

The cultural relics were unloaded in the afternoon and still hired more than a dozen trucks to transport them to the building at No. 26 Catholic Church Street for storage. By 7:00 PM, 30% had been unloaded. It is said that unloading will begin at 6:00 AM this morning to complete the unloading in one day.

Fifth Batch Awaiting Transport 147

According to Deputy Director Ma, there is still a fifth batch of cultural relics awaiting transport, including 3,000 boxes from the Cultural Relics Exhibition Hall and 1,000 boxes from the Palace Museum, totaling 4,000 boxes. Cars have been sent, and they will be transported here in a week.

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Sent a Letter to the Telephone Bureau Requesting Exemption from Additional Telephone Charges

From Six Dollars to Ten Dollars: The Public's Financial Burden is Truly Insurmountable 148

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Shanghai Telephone Bureau yesterday, requesting the exemption of telephone fee increases. The original text stated: According to a letter from the Shanghai Restaurant Trade Association, members of the Zhabei Greater China and other establishments reported that the North and South City Chinese telephone bureaus, disregarding commercial conditions, have replaced their equipment and taken the opportunity to increase prices, which were announced to take effect on May 1st. Since the January 28th Incident, the disaster areas have not yet recovered, and the original telephone fee was six dollars per household, which has now been increased to ten dollars. At a time when business is sluggish, this sudden doubling of telephone fees is a burden that merchants and residents cannot bear. They requested that the matter be negotiated with the bureau to cancel the price increase and continue charging the original price, in order to alleviate the merchants' difficulties and prevent their downfall. This matter was referred to the Executive Committee for discussion on the 23rd of this month, and it was resolved to first send a letter to your esteemed organization for review, to argue strongly for the cancellation of the price increase with the telephone bureau, and to continue charging the original price, in order to alleviate the merchants' plight and save them from impending disaster. This is of great importance. In view of this, it is evident that the city's commercial stagnation since the January 28th Incident last year is obvious to all, especially in the Chinese areas of the North and South Cities. Telephones are a necessity for business, and now the cost per household has increased to ten dollars, which is several times more than the previous six dollars per household. At a time when the productivity of citizens is declining, it is truly difficult to bear. Accordingly, this matter is reported and conveyed, and it is hoped that your esteemed bureau will take this into consideration and exempt the aforementioned fee increase, in order to strengthen public relations.

Following the Telephone Bureau's Installation of Automatic Switching Equipment

A History of Telephones 149

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications was established in the twenty-eighth year of the Guangxu reign of the late Qing Dynasty. At the time of its establishment, it only rented three floors in a civilian house on Xinmatou Li Street as its office. It housed 480 manual switchboard lines, and there were only over 200 subscribers at the time. Later, the number gradually increased to over 400. In the ninth year of the Republic, the bureau purchased land on Zhonghua Road, Dananmen, and built its own office, switching room, storage room, and staff dormitory. It also ordered 2,000 common battery switchboard lines from the United States, installed underground cables, and reconstructed overhead lines, thus achieving a rudimentary scale. Subsequently, the Zhabei, Jiangwan, Longhua, Nanxiang, and Wusong branch offices were successively established. In the fourteenth year of the Republic, a contract was signed with the China and Foreign Telephone Company to allow telephone communication between the Chinese and foreign concession areas, which was convenient for the citizens. In the fifteenth year, the Shanghai-Xichang long-distance line was completed, marking the beginning of telephone communication between Beijing and Shanghai. In the eighteenth year, the Ministry of Communications signed a contract with the China Automatic Telephone Company, and added new Zhabei and Pudong bureau sites on Yongxing Road and Dongchang Road in Zhabei and Pudong respectively. The Nanshi, Zhabei, and Pudong bureaus were converted to Strowger automatic telephones, with 3,000 lines in Nanshi, 1,500 lines in Zhabei, and 300 lines in Pudong, totaling 4,800 lines. The total price of all automatic equipment and line materials was US$570,000.

Recent Developments 150

After the Ministry of Communications signed a contract with the China Automatic Telephone Company to purchase automatic equipment, it signed another contract with the company in May of the nineteenth year to build the Zhabei and Pudong bureau buildings. In April of that year, the company began shipping automatic equipment materials to Shanghai in batches. In September, installation began at the Nanshi Main Bureau. In the twentieth year, the Zhabei and Pudong bureau buildings were completed. By December of that year, the automatic equipment in Nanshi and Zhabei had been installed. However, the Ministry of Communications realized that automatic telephones required not only excellent internal equipment but also perfect external lines. Therefore, it specifically ordered the Shanghai Telephone Bureau to construct 1,660 meters of underground conduits in the Nanshi district and 3,520 meters of underground conduits in the Zhabei district, and to add overhead cables to shorten open-wire lines in order to reduce interference. This project was very time-consuming. Unexpectedly, just as the various projects were nearing completion, the January 28th Incident suddenly broke out. The automatic equipment and line projects of the Zhabei branch were destroyed, and the underground cables and pole materials stored in the material warehouse were reduced to ashes. The project was greatly hampered. As a result, materials from Nanshi and Pudong were transported to supplement and repair the project, which was barely completed in early April. These are the developments of the past three years.

Ordering Telephones 151

Since the automatic equipment in Nanshi and Zhabei had been completed and the external lines had also been completed, the Ministry of Communications repeatedly ordered the bureau to expedite the work and prepare for telephone service in the Nanshi and Zhabei districts as soon as possible for the convenience of the Shanghai citizens. Therefore, the bureau rushed to work internally and externally for several days and finally opened telephone service on April 15th. However, although the internal automatic equipment of the Pudong branch had also been installed, most of the external line materials had been moved to Nanshi and Zhabei and could not be replenished. Therefore, telephone service could not be opened at the same time. The Ministry of Communications is now trying to order materials. As soon as they arrive, the bureau will be ordered to start work and it will soon be completed.

Increasing Trunk Lines 152

Shanghai is a major trading port, and the concession is the center. Among the bureau's subscribers, seven or eight out of ten communicate with telephones in the concession. Therefore, communication between the Chinese and foreign concession areas is the biggest problem. The bureau and the Shanghai Telephone Company originally had 24 pairs of incoming and outgoing trunk lines and 6 pairs of long-distance trunk lines, all included. After the automatic telephone service was implemented, the number of incoming and outgoing trunk lines was increased to 30 pairs each. The incoming trunk lines from all directions were directly connected to the automatic equipment, eliminating the trouble of switching through the switchboard, so that both parties improved. The long-distance station of the Nanshi Main Bureau was moved to the new Zhabei Bureau, and another 8 pairs of trunk lines were set up. Therefore, the communication of the public has become more agile than before. The bureau has asked the Shanghai Telephone Company to continue to increase the equipment for the trunk lines and to cancel the three-minute limit and the five-cent fee for the ocean. The company did not agree because of the greater losses and insufficient equipment. If it can be successful in the future, then the public will be even more convenient to communicate.

Renting Trunk Lines 153

There were originally 19 pairs of trunk lines between Nanshi and Zhabei. Recently, due to the development of business, the number of trunk lines was insufficient. It was originally planned to rent 100 pairs, but the rental price has increased several times compared to before. Only 30 pairs were rented. This is because the lines are completely rented from the Shanghai Telephone Company. The original rent was 50 taels per pair per year. Now the company must pay an annual rent of 200 taels per pair according to the newly established price, which is four times the original price. The Ministry of Communications repeatedly ordered the bureau to negotiate with the Shanghai Telephone Company to reduce the price, but it did not succeed. However, for the convenience of the citizens, the bureau was ordered to rent 30 pairs at the price first, so that communication between the two places would not be delayed due to congestion.

Reasons for the Price Increase 154

The bureau ordered automatic equipment, and the capital expenditure was enormous. Moreover, the price of gold has risen sharply, doubling from what it used to be. The annual rent for the trunk lines has also increased from 50 taels to 200 taels. In addition, long-distance and Chinese-foreign concession communication still require the connection of operators. Therefore, the various maintenance costs continue to increase, and there is a real danger of being unable to make ends meet. Moreover, after the automatic telephone service started, according to the contract, a bonus of 4,000 yuan, equivalent to about 20,000 Chinese currency, must be paid to the China Automatic Telephone Company every month. The expenditure has increased sharply, so the telephone price has been appropriately increased to provide some support. However, due to the commercial depression in Shanghai after the January 28th Incident, the Ministry of Communications, in order to show consideration for the citizens, specially reduced the monthly rent for automatic telephones in the bureau by one yuan compared to the capital. The Longhua, Jiangwan, Zhenru, and Wusong areas where automatic telephones have not been installed will continue to be handled according to the old rules, in order to relieve the burden on the citizens.

Ongoing Work 155

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau is a national enterprise and should abide by the Ministry's regulations, strive to implement them, and refer to commercial practices to become fully commercialized. Therefore, the planning of projects, the review of materials, the assessment of employees, the development of business, the economy of facilities, and the convenience of the public must be carefully studied and improved. Now the bureau's Nanshi and Zhabei automatic equipment conversion projects have been completed, and the Pudong branch will also begin work. The equipment and lines have been gradually improved, and the capital costs have also increased accordingly. It is reported that the bureau is improving the city's telephone services. If direct Chinese-foreign communication is possible, then the public will feel much more convenient at that time.

The original text stated: (For compliance, it is found that the implementation of factory inspections is an important part of labor administration. Since the Ministry was ordered by the National Government to promulgate the Factory Inspection Law, it has repeatedly consulted the provincial and municipal governments to instruct the competent authorities to earnestly organize the inspections, and the Ministry has formulated the Regulations on the Appointment, Rewards and Punishments of Factory Inspectors and the Statistical Table of Factory Inspection Rewards, which have been promulgated in the past. If the local competent authorities can strictly enforce factory inspections at ordinary times and strictly supervise the various factories, they will not cause this accident. Therefore, the factory inspection is really not allowed to be delayed any longer. In the future, the competent authorities should take the tragic accident in the Zhengtai Factory in Shanghai as a warning, urge factory inspections, and earnestly organize them at any time in accordance with the provisions of the Factory Inspection Law, and prepare a detailed plan for the implementation of factory inspections and submit it to the Ministry for verification. Workers Oppose Suspension of Work and Salary Reduction

Workers from Yongyu, Tianyi, Siyi Factories Petition Party and Government Agencies Yesterday Morning 165

Our country's silk yarn factories have been affected by the economic panic and business is sluggish, resulting in suspension of work and salary reduction. On the other hand, the workers are concerned about their livelihoods. Once they lose their jobs, they lack the means to make a living, and labor-management disputes are increasing day by day. Yesterday, workers from Yongyu, Tianyi, Siyi factories petitioned party and government agencies. They are recorded as follows:

Yongyu Yarn Factory 166

The Yongyu Heji Yarn Factory on Guangfu Road, Zhabei, has a total of more than 3,800 weavers. Recently, the factory claimed that it was operating at a loss and that its economic turnover was not flexible, so it closed the factory on the 6th of this month. All the workers, with their livelihoods in trouble, petitioned the municipal government and the municipal party headquarters. However, after two weeks, there was no movement. Yesterday morning at 10 o'clock, five representatives, Yin Zhen, Jing Yunlong, You Jinxiang, Fang Xiangming, and Cui Jinhou, went to the municipal party headquarters to petition, requesting early mediation. Lu Yinchu of the Civil Training Department received them and promised to handle it together with the Social Bureau. Then they went to the Social Bureau to petition, and Zhang Chuqiang, a mediator, received them and promised to handle it immediately after asking for instructions.

Tianyi Silk Factory 167

The Tianyi Silk Factory on Zhengsheng Road, Tilanqiao, Hudong, has a total of more than 200 male and female workers. Recently, they opposed the factory's reduction of original wages, changing to an 80% calculation, and the cancellation of the subsidy of 50 cents per person per day for warp and weft and the old practice of a monthly bonus of one yuan per person, which aroused the opposition of all the workers. They petitioned the Social Bureau on the 23rd, but no mediation has been made. The factory has declared that if any workers object, they will be dismissed. The workers were panic-stricken and held a petition flag and petitioned the Social Bureau yesterday morning at 10:40, demanding protection and immediate mediation. Wang Xianqing, director of the Mediation Section, received them and appointed mediator Tan Peiyan to go to investigate at 1:00 p.m. and scheduled a hearing for both parties at 9:00 a.m. this morning.

Siyi Silk Factory 168

The Siyi Factory on Zhoujiazui Road suspended work on March 13 due to sluggish business. The Social Bureau mediated and agreed on a method allowing the capital side to suspend work for 40 days, until the end of April. In May, work will resume as usual. Now the capital side has notified the workers that, due to inflexible capital turnover and the impact of the current situation on silk merchants, they cannot resume work. For the sake of the workers' lives, they have applied to the Social Bureau for legal dismissal. This aroused the opposition of the workers, who sent representatives Yu Fuli, Chen Biheng, Zhu Ali, and Gong Zhangsen to the Social Bureau to petition for relief yesterday morning. Mediator Tan Peiyan received them and said that since the capital side could not continue to operate, it would be difficult to force them. Both parties will be summoned on a scheduled basis to carry out dismissal procedures.

The Story of the Mercy and Child Welfare Association's Relief of Dai Caixin 169

On February 3rd of this year, a woman named Dai Caixin complained to the China Mercy and Child Welfare Association. She claimed that she was 20 years old, from Ningbo, and lost her mother at the age of three. She was raised by her grandmother. At the age of 18, she came to Shanghai with her father and stepmother, Dai Yao. Because her father, Dai Mingguan, did not work properly, spent day and night with villains, and indulged in smoking, drinking, and gambling, the family became destitute. Listening to the instigation of her stepmother, she followed the evil plan of the gangsters and decided to sell her to Hankou as a prostitute. She had negotiated prices twice in the Guifangge teahouse in Hongkou and had drafted a sales contract for 600 yuan. Knowing that disaster was imminent, the woman had no choice but to resist her father and elope to Ningbo. She wept to her relatives and friends, but none of them dared to agree because they were afraid of Dai's evil. The woman had no choice but to take the opportunity to hang herself and escape, reporting to the association to request relief. The association immediately assigned the protection officer Wang Guanyi to investigate the matter and learned the truth. On the one hand, he reported and registered to the Hua Jun, the district chief of the Huishan Police Station where her father lived, and because the woman's age was not in line with the regulations of the association's attached educational institute, it was difficult to accommodate her. He then inquired whether Caixin had any relatives and friends in Shanghai. It was said that although there were several relatives and friends in Shanghai, they were all afraid of Dai's wickedness and dared not hear about it. Only her uncle Jiang Zhuoying, who had moved from Suzhou to Shanghai due to (reason), and whose address had not yet been known to Dai, might be willing to accommodate her temporarily. Therefore, officer Wang set out to verify that Jiang was a former employee of the Sanyou Industrial Company and now runs the Dahua Cotton Weaving Factory in Shanghai, with a wife and daughter, and is extremely kind. He asked if Jiang would agree to temporarily entrust Xin Cai to him. Jiang and his wife were initially suspicious and afraid, and dared not rashly agree. Later, it was explained that this was a temporary entrustment and could be resolved immediately, and the association could keep the address temporarily confidential to avoid trouble. Therefore, Jiang and his wife reluctantly agreed. The association immediately completed the entrustment of Caixin, and immediately informed her grandmother in Ningbo and summoned her father to the association to start mediation, in order to reconcile the father and daughter and ensure that she would not be sold. Her father went to the association several times, but in the end, with a cunning and stubborn attitude, he refused to mediate and insisted on getting interest from his daughter. The association was about to send him to the police station for legal action, but he fled to Ningbo and threatened his relatives and friends, demanding that they hand over the woman. Otherwise, he would destroy the furniture and take the clothes to pawn. This matter was most serious in his brother Dai Manguan's place. Xia Guan had no choice but to travel back and forth between Shanghai and Ningbo, visiting various relatives and friends, and inadvertently met Jiang Zhuoying. He told the truth, and in order to avoid hurting the feelings of his brothers, Xia Guan told Mingguan Jiang's address. Mingguan privately took Jiang and his wife to the (district) office without the knowledge of the association, accusing them of abducting Caixin, and made false statements and reversed the facts. After the association was notified by the office, it sent officer Wang to rush to prove everything. The Public Security Bureau sent a document to the Shanghai Local Court, and after the investigation, Jiang and his wife were released, and Dai Mingguan was dealt with according to law. With the consent of the Mercy and Child Welfare Association, Caixin was transferred to the China Women and Children Relief Association. The association believes that this case has caused a lot of trouble to Jiang and his wife. In addition to asking them to write to various newspapers to correct the matter, the facts are recorded above.

The Examination of the Case of the Chinese Police Shooting and Killing the Head Constable and Then Killing Himself 170

丨The Two Corpses Were Each Claimed by Their Wives丨

Li Chunhe, No. 1889, a Chinese constable from Shandong Province in the Desserve Way Police Station, 32 years old, had hatred with Song Huchen, No. 322, a Chinese constable from the same row, 37 years old. The estimated expenses included 75,000 yuan for the China Pavilion, 15,000 yuan for decoration, 30,000 yuan for transportation, 10,000 yuan for promotion, 10,000 yuan for entertainment and Commissioner Zhang's travel expenses, and 10,000 yuan for reserve funds, totaling 150,000 yuan. The government allocated 50,000 yuan in subsidies, the exhibitors contributed 60,000 yuan, and various provinces and cities assisted with 15,000 yuan, totaling 125,000 yuan. The missing 25,000 yuan was borrowed by Director Lin Kanghou from the banking sector in the city, to be repaid after the exposition concludes from the proceeds of the sale of the exhibits in the United States.

今日啟運 173

The Chicago Exposition is scheduled to open on June 1st. The China Pavilion has already begun construction by Commissioner Zhang after arriving in the United States, and is expected to be completed by May 20th. As for the exhibits to be included, it has been decided to load them onto the Great Lai Company's President Lincoln today, which will set sail for the United States tomorrow morning, totaling 400 boxes. Furthermore, the exhibitors, including Zhou Guanhong, are also scheduled to take the President Lincoln to the United States tonight, with all travel expenses borne by themselves. This time, the exhibitors have independently planned and achieved the goal of autonomous participation, which is truly not an easy task.

名貴出品 174

The exhibits to be included are porcelain, lacquerware, pottery, Xiang embroidery, jade, antiques, etc., with porcelain being the most numerous. All are quite precious. Among the jade products exhibited by Suzhou jade merchant Zhang Wenti, the jade pagoda carved from raw jade is the most valuable, priceless, and took ten years and nine months to complete. It is about five feet high, with seven stories, palace rooms, transparent and luminous. It was not displayed at the exhibition of exhibits because it was too precious. Secondly, the carved Yang Guifei palace lanterns are also famous, rare, and valuable items.

Appeal Verdict in the Le Zhenbao Kidnapping Case

二人减處徒刑二人維持原判 175

Le Zhenbao, the owner of Taichang Woodware Store, was kidnapped by bandits on December 9th of last year, who demanded a large ransom. Subsequently, Chief Detective You A'gen of the Old Zhabei Police Station managed to detect the bandits' den, rescued Le, and arrested many kidnappers. Six guns, including gas pistols and Mauser pistols, and more than 260 rounds of ammunition were seized. They were handed over to the First Special District Local Court for investigation and conclusion. Ma Gensheng, Guan Afu, and Ren Zixiang were sentenced to death; Cao Ziqing, Jin Zipei, and Wang Xiaosizi were sentenced to life imprisonment; Hu Hongsheng was sentenced to 20 years imprisonment; Li Youren and Zhou Jinsheng were sentenced to 13 years imprisonment each; Cao Ziyu and Pan Yaoming were sentenced to 7 years imprisonment each. The guns and ammunition were confiscated. However, the bandits sentenced to death and life imprisonment were not satisfied with the first instance verdict and filed an appeal. Among those sentenced to imprisonment, Li Youren also filed an appeal. Previously, the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court opened a hearing. When the cases of the appellants were investigated, Cao Ziqing hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to defend him. Based on various reasons, he argued that the original sentence of life imprisonment was inappropriate and requested a revised verdict. Some of the other appellants also hired lawyers to defend them. Yesterday afternoon, the date for the verdict was announced. Police lawyer Gan Jingxian and the lawyers of the appellants appeared in court to await the announcement. Subsequently, Judge Zhao and Assessors Zhou and Jiang took their seats and announced the verdict: Cao Ziqing and Wang Xiaosizi were both reduced to 15 years imprisonment. The appeals of Jin Zipei and Li Youren were rejected, and the original sentences were upheld. Ma Gensheng, Guan Afu, and Ren Zixiang were convicted according to the Law for the Punishment of Bandits, and according to the law, they had no right to appeal, so their appeals were also rejected.

顓橋作息鐘 176

丨昨行揭幕禮丨

The Zhuangqiao Farmers' Education Center in Shanghai County, recognizing the importance of setting up a time bell, in addition to submitting a request to the county to designate the ancient bell of Mingxin Temple in Beiqiao as the new Zhuangqiao time bell, also raised funds to set up a time bell in Zhuangqiao. Now, after Director Zhang raised the funds, the bell tower has been purchased and construction completed. The unveiling ceremony was held yesterday, and the bell will be struck every day according to the scheduled time to awaken the people.

拘獲女共產黨 177

丨長沙人張秀蘭丨

Wen Hong'en, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, recently received a tip that a female Communist Party member from Changsha, Zhang Xiulan, also known as Huang Li, 29 years old, was hiding at No. 9, Lane 729, Avenue des Soeurs, in the French Concession, secretly working in Shanghai. Director Wen, upon receiving the report, prepared a document and dispatched personnel to the French Concession Police on the morning of the day before yesterday to request assistance in arresting and transferring her. The Political Department sent Chinese and foreign detectives to the address to arrest Zhang and confiscate documents and books. She was taken to the police station. The next afternoon, she was escorted to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court for interrogation. At 3:30, Criminal Judge Zhou Yunhui, accompanied by Assessors Guo Dezhang and Fan Peien, together with the prosecutor, opened the Criminal Court Three for interrogation. Police lawyer Yao Zhaodi appeared in court and requested a postponement for investigation. The Public Security Bureau also sent personnel to the case, requesting the transfer. Because the court declared that the case was political, listening was prohibited. According to the results of the interrogation, the court ordered a change of date for further investigation, and the defendant was returned to custody to await further instructions.

The Shanghai Muslim community previously proposed to rename Fangbang Road in the Nanshi district to Andexin Road in memory of Battalion Commander Andexin, a martyr of the Battle of Yuguan, in order to commemorate him and comfort his loyal soul. The Bureau of Public Works replied that the road name already had a considerable history, and changing the name would be very troublesome.
